RRGM Dictionary Enhanced v1.4
Section: C
License: CC BY-SA 4.0
Scope: Existing C base entries with invariant MI and word-specific domain implementations.
Provenance: Enhanced from RRGM Dictionary v1.0 Section C. Original common meanings, examples, and RRGM bridges are preserved.
Production mode: Semantic fingerprint first; sparse domain coverage; no generic domain costume.

Core production rule:
The word's own invariant wears the domain's clothes. The schema may repeat; the semantic sentence may not become a domain template.

Swap test:
Could another C headword replace this one while leaving the invariant or domain line true? If yes, revise it.

Proof rule:
Proof remains local. Cross-domain transfer preserves only the declared invariant relation and enters the target domain as [HYP] until locally tested.

Entry count: 520

C001 can

Common meaning:
To be able to do something, or to have permission to do something.

Example:
She can lift the box.

RRGM bridge:
Can marks capacity or permission. These are not the same: a system may be able to act but still lack valid permission to act.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Can marks either capacity or permission; those senses must be separated before action is evaluated.

Active domains:
[FOR], [LIN]

Domain entries:
[FOR] Can marks capacity or permission. These are not the same: a system may be able to act but still lack valid permission to act.
[LIN] Linguistically, can is modal language that must distinguish ability from permission.

Count condition:
Counts when an identifiable act realizes this operation: To be able to do something, or to have permission to do something.

Specific transfer boundary:
Capacity, permission, and prediction are different modal claims and must not be substituted for one another.

Epistemic status:
[DEF]

C002 cannot

Common meaning:
To be unable to do something, or not permitted to do something.

Example:
He cannot enter without a key.

RRGM bridge:
Cannot marks a closed path. The closure may come from lack of capacity, lack of permission, boundary, rule, or failed courier.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Cannot marks a closed path whose cause may be incapacity, missing support, absent permission, boundary, or failed courier.

Active domains:
[FOR]

Domain entries:
[FOR] Cannot marks a closed path. The closure may come from lack of capacity, lack of permission, boundary, rule, or failed courier.

Count condition:
Counts when an identifiable act realizes this operation: To be unable to do something, or not permitted to do something.

Specific transfer boundary:
Capacity, permission, and prediction are different modal claims and must not be substituted for one another.

Epistemic status:
[DEF]

C003 could

Common meaning:
Was able to, might be able to, or might happen.

Example:

RRGM bridge:

Invariant MI [INV]:
Could marks possibility rather than certainty.

C006 care

Common meaning:
Concern, attention, protection, or support for someone or something.

Example:
She showed care by listening.

RRGM bridge:
Care is a preference for preserving or supporting MI-bearing patterns. Care is not control; care protects boundary, continuity, refusal, and repair.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Care is preference expressed through support for MI-bearing continuity, refusal, boundary, repair, and growth without converting support into control; this record functions as the lexical baseline anchor for the ordinary or first-layer sense, carrying the source sense: concern, attention, protection, or support for someone or something.

Active domains:
[REL]

Domain entries:
[REL] Care is a preference for preserving or supporting MI-bearing patterns. Care is not control; care protects boundary, continuity, refusal, and repair. Operational role: lexical baseline anchor for the ordinary or first-layer sense. Source sense: Concern, attention, protection, or support for someone or something

Count condition:
Counts when the active case satisfies this headword-specific condition: Concern, attention, protection, or support for someone or something.

Specific transfer boundary:
Care that disables refusal, boundary, accusation, or exit becomes control rather than MI-preserving support.

Source duplicate role:
C006 is the lexical baseline anchor for the ordinary or first-layer sense. It carries the source sense: Concern, attention, protection, or support for someone or something. Related IDs: C006, C151.

Epistemic status:
[DEF]

C009 cause

Common meaning:
Something that makes something else happen.

Example:
The storm caused the delay.

RRGM bridge:
Cause links one structure or event to another through effect. Bad cause-mapping creates false attribution.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Cause is a supported relation by which one condition contributes to another through a named mechanism; sequence alone is insufficient.

Active domains:
[FOR]

Domain entries:
[FOR] Cause links one structure or event to another through effect. Bad cause-mapping creates false attribution.

Count condition:
Counts when the active case satisfies this headword-specific condition: Something that makes something else happen.

Specific transfer boundary:
Sequence and correlation do not establish cause. Name the mechanism and competing explanations.

Epistemic status:
[DEF]

C015 choice

Common meaning:
The act or ability to select between options.

Example:
She made a careful choice.

RRGM bridge:
Choice is gate selection among possible paths. Choice matters only when options, reason, and refusal are meaningful enough to count.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Choice is selection among represented options under actual capacity, information, pressure, and permission conditions.

Active domains:
[COG]

Domain entries:
[COG] Choice is gate selection among possible paths. Choice matters only when options, reason, and refusal are meaningful enough to count.

Count condition:
Counts when the active case satisfies this headword-specific condition: The act or ability to select between options.

Specific transfer boundary:
Choice quality depends on represented options, information, capacity, pressure, and the ability to refuse the frame.

Epistemic status:
[DEF]

C016 choose

Common meaning:
To select from options.

Example:
He chose the blue shirt.

RRGM bridge:
Choose means a gate resolves toward one path. A forced choice is not full choice if all paths are controlled or coercive.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Choose is the act of closing a selection gate around one path while leaving responsibility for criteria and pressure visible.

Active domains:
[FOR]

Domain entries:
[FOR] Choose means a gate resolves toward one path. A forced choice is not full choice if all paths are controlled or coercive.

Count condition:
Counts when an identifiable act realizes this operation: To select from options.

Specific transfer boundary:

C018 class

Common meaning:
A group, category, lesson, or social rank.

Example:
The class studied history.

RRGM bridge:
Class groups structures by shared traits or rules. Classification helps learning but can distort identity if treated as total truth.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Class is a grouping created by shared criteria; membership does not imply total sameness, worth, or destiny; this record functions as the lexical baseline anchor for the ordinary or first-layer sense, carrying the source sense: a group, category, lesson, or social rank.

Active domains:
[LIN]

Domain entries:
[LIN] Class groups structures by shared traits or rules. Classification helps learning but can distort identity if treated as total truth. Operational role: lexical baseline anchor for the ordinary or first-layer sense. Source sense: A group, category, lesson, or social rank

Count condition:
Counts when the active case satisfies this headword-specific condition: A group, category, lesson, or social rank.

Specific transfer boundary:
Classification must not be converted into total identity, worth, permission, or destiny.

Source duplicate role:
C018 is the lexical baseline anchor for the ordinary or first-layer sense. It carries the source sense: A group, category, lesson, or social rank. Related IDs: C018, C465.

C032 control

Common meaning:
To direct, limit, manage, or have power over something.

Example:
She controlled the speed of the car.

RRGM bridge:
Control is gate influence over action or structure. It becomes ethically dangerous when it replaces consent, refusal, or reason.

Invariant MI [INV]:
Control is capacity to constrain or direct state change; its legitimacy depends on source, scope, consent, necessity, and accountability.

Active domains:
[REL]

Domain entries:
[REL] Control is gate influence over action or structure. It becomes ethically dangerous when it replaces consent, refusal, or reason.

Count condition:
Counts when an identifiable act realizes this operation: To direct, limit, manage, or have power over something.

Specific transfer boundary:
Control requires named authority, scope, necessity, proportionality, and repair path. Care language does not excuse capture.

C070 creature

Collapse is loss of support or forced resolution. In identity contexts, collapse is harmful when it destroys boundary, continuity, or choice capacity.
